      2013 Immortals After Dark series reread with IAD group
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=alpha-hero">alpha-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=bad-boy-rake-or-rogue">bad-boy-rake-or-rogue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=celibate-or-less-experienced-hero">celibate-or-less-experienced-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fated-to-be-mated">fated-to-be-mated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-in-pursuit">hero-in-pursuit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-to-die-for">hero-to-die-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-loved">heroine-i-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=kickbutt-heroine">kickbutt-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=werewolf">werewolf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35542629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5301282238758873073"><br/>This is my second read of this book, and my first attempt to review it. I couldn’t write a review before, because it had been years since I read it, and my feelings were so all over the place. I didn’t think I could write an honest review at the time unless I did reread it. Don’t get me wrong. I love this book, and it’s definitely a five star read, but it challenged me in ways the first three books didn’t.<br/><br/>Bowen is a character we got to know in A Hunger Like No Other, and we followed up on him in</span>
  <span id="freeText5301282238758873073" style="display:none"><br />This is my second read of this book, and my first attempt to review it. I couldn’t write a review before, because it had been years since I read it, and my feelings were so all over the place. I didn’t think I could write an honest review at the time unless I did reread it. Don’t get me wrong. I love this book, and it’s definitely a five star read, but it challenged me in ways the first three books didn’t.<br /><br />Bowen is a character we got to know in A Hunger Like No Other, and we followed up on him in No Rest for the Wicked. I was already emotionally involved with him, so it was exciting for him to get his own story. Despite that fact, Bowen could be a major jerk at times. I mean a serious clod. Some of the thoughtless things he says and does towards Mariketa are just loutish. I really winced at one particular misstep. An epic fail. I was just thinking: Wow, Bowen. You’re like the guy who caught the ball that cost the Cubs their first chance at the World Series in a long time! Yeah, that bad!<br /><br />Despite the fact that Bowen commits some serious relationship nonos with Mariketa, he also has some heart-meltingly sweet moments where you can’t imagine not being bowled over by a guy like him wooing you. I think that combination of ineptness and fan yourself appealing hotness makes him an unforgettable hero. It means so much that despite the numerous obstacles he faces in his relationship with Mariketa, that he is able to win her heart and keep it, and leave behind all his preconceived notions and reservations about being involved with her. And I can’t blame him for some of those, just about how insensitive he was in addressing or dealing with them.<br /><br />Mariketa is quite interesting as a heroine. Although she’s younger than Emmaline, she’s a lot more modern-thinking and less sheltered. She embodies the modern twenties-something girl in a more recognizable way than Emmaline, although they both have that dynamic. I liked that she was more street-smart than Emmaline because Bowen really needed someone who could handle him. Now, that’s not to say that he doesn’t wound Mariketa, or sorely challenge her. At times, I could see why Mariketa definitely was not feeling the idea of a relationship with him. She had very good reasons, especially with her abandonment/not measuring up issues and his disdain for witches. On the second read, I was cheering her on a lot more. When she called him on his selfishness, she hit the nail right on the head. I could see why she wasn’t about to let her sexual attraction and maybe a little more feelings for Bowen deter her from the path she’d chosen, especially when Bowen felt like she had to give up something that was so vital to her identity.<br /><br />It struck me that this book has a lot more relationship drama than the previous books. I think that although this is paranormal, some of the relationship dynamics would feel very familiar to a modern person with an active dating life; and they are trying to decide if someone is the ‘one’ they want to spend their life with. Many readers seem to dislike the ‘love at first/fated to be mated’ concept, but Cole doesn’t use it as a crutch to get out of building a genuine bond between her characters, or as a foregone conclusion. They still have to work out and through the particulars of cementing and committing to that relationship despite their instincts that they belong together. Particularly in this book, I seriously wondered how Mariketa and Bowen would work things out. Their problems are pretty enormous despite their volcanic sexual chemistry and growing love for each other. Since this is a romance, logically I know we’ll get a happy ending, but there is a good haul to get to that destination.<br /><br />As always, Cole blisters the pages with the powerful sexual chemistry between her characters. She tantalizes and teases the reader so that they are just as highly expectant for the promised consummation as her main characters. And she doesn’t disappoint when it happens. I love the fact that Mariketa doesn’t make it easy for Bowen sexually. She needs his respect as much as the sexual release he clearly can give her. She also needs trust, and that is something a reader can definitely identify with. It just feels right. Even though the reader can love all the hot stuff, you can also get a connection between the main characters that makes sense intellectually and ethically (if that makes sense). You don’t want a character who doesn’t respect herself enough to expect respect from a hero.<br /><br />Wow, this review turned out pretty long. I guess I did have a lot to say. Everything I love about Cole’s writing is here. She challenges me in ways, but that’s good. While this book has a bit more angst than the first three books, it also has some good humorous bits. The suspense storyline is intense, and it ties together very well. I liked that I didn’t remember exactly how everything goes together, which is a mark of a good book, that you can see more in the story with each read. Wicked Deeds on a Winter’s Night is a worthwhile read for fans of well-written, sexy paranormal romance. <br /><br />Final Shoutout: Bowen, I’m glad you finally got your act together. High five! Mariketa, you go girl!<br /><br />Check out my <a href="http://pinterest.com/gatadelafuente/immortals-after-dark-series-by-kresley-cole/" rel="nofollow noopener">Immortals After Dark Pinboard</a> on Pinterest!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5301282238758873073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14439184998415839231" style="display:none">Get out the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50786.Men_in_Kilts" title="Men in Kilts by Katie MacAlister" rel="nofollow noopener">men in kilts</a> and the bagpipes and put me on the next plane to Scotland! Looks like he is trying to win that slot again.<br/><br/>Robert Petkoff is wonderful at infusing life and <i>emotions</i> into Ms. Cole’s amazing characters. Oh, he is certainly <b>D</b>elicious with the Scottish accent. Not only that, he differentiates the member of the Lykae </span>
  <span id="freeText11047682066253252328" style="display:none"><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1339297342p8/514006.jpg" width="225" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>★★★★★ (This is a review of the audiobook.) Man-oh-man-oh-man-man! This one is so well narrated by <b>Robert Petkoff</b>. I hope he is doing them all. Looks like he is trying to win that slot again.<br><br>Robert Petkoff is wonderful at infusing life and <i>emotions</i> into Ms. Cole’s amazing characters. Oh, he is certainly <b>D</b>elicious with the Scottish accent. Not only that, he differentiates the member of the Lykae clan, all Scottish, so that you’re not confused when Bowen and Lachlain are in a conversation together. Nevertheless, one scene I just marveled at was when Mariketa was mimicking Bowen’s accent. Too funny! How did Mr. Petkoff manage that? LOL!<br><br>Mr. Petkoff also made Cadeon Woede, with a lovely English accent, sound yummy, too! I can NOT wait for that one (#6) to be released. <br><br>My heart always ached for Bowen MacRieve; having lost his mate over two centuries ago, in the previous installments of this wonderful paranormal series he pretty much didn’t care if he lived or died. However, with an opportunity to bring his intended mate back with a prize won in the Hie, he has a mission. Watch out for a Lykae on a mission!<br><br>Then he runs into Mariketa the Awaited – or Mari - a pretty little redheaded witch he is sure has been practicing magic on him, since he is wildly attracted to her. Bowen, believing she has toyed with him, enthralled him, does the unthinkable and traps Mari and a few other Hie competitors in a Guatemalan tomb with some swarming incubi! Eep! <br><br>But that is just the start of it. Mari really does put a spell on him just as he is making his exit, and what a spell it is. Oh the twists and turns in this one are great! Only Ms. Cole could write Bowen out of all the mistakes he makes.<br><br>The fourth in the <i>Immortal After Dark</i> series is one of my favorite. Love Bowen and Maiketa’s story! If you need a refresher on what happened in the past books, why not listen to it on audio? (Includes Immortals After Dark, #8; Alien Huntress, #4.5) by Kresley Cole" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a <div id="review_125749924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125749924" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125749924?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kresley Cole fans and paranormal romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=drinks-on-me">drinks-on-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers">keep-a-spare-pair-of-knickers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=mages-or-witches">mages-or-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-kresley-cole">author-kresley-cole</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125749924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13672308500207990291">Wicked Deeds on a Winter’s Night is the third book in the Immortals After Dark series. It features Bowen McReieve, a heartbroken Lykae who lost his mate over two centuries ago and is still feeling the guilt because he believes he caused her death. The heroine is a fiery, snarky little witch named Mariketa. <br/><br/>When the two of them compete in the Hie, Bowe tries desperately to win so that he can bring back his former paramour, Mariah back to life. In the process, he traps Mari and some other friends </span>
  <span id="freeText13672308500207990291" style="display:none">Wicked Deeds on a Winter’s Night is the third book in the Immortals After Dark series. It features Bowen McReieve, a heartbroken Lykae who lost his mate over two centuries ago and is still feeling the guilt because he believes he caused her death. The heroine is a fiery, snarky little witch named Mariketa. <br /><br />When the two of them compete in the Hie, Bowe tries desperately to win so that he can bring back his former paramour, Mariah back to life. In the process, he traps Mari and some other friends in a tomb while he goes for the big prize. But he loses to a vampire and gets stranded for a week. He realizes that with each passing moment, all he thinks about is the little witch and comes to the conclusion that she put an enchantment on him. Turns out that Mari and her friends are still trapped in the tomb with nasty incubi and Bowen must free her in order for her to remove the spell. And that’s when all the fun begins because naturally, Mari is pissed as hell and there is no way she’s taking crap from a werewolf.<br /><br />Bowen and Mari are wonderful together. Their love/hate relationship is so entertaining and downright hilarious! Their banter is enough to keep me reading for hours. But in addition to the great chemistry, Cole does a great job with her world building and character development. Bowe is a total package with the Scottish accent (though I had a hard time reading it at first, but it’s dead sexy) and dark possessiveness and Mari is a strong modern girl that shines in comparison to the plain and proper, Mariah. <br /><br />And when they get down to it, things are steeeeamy! BUT when Bowe yells out MARIAH instead of Mariketa’s name during the act, things get sour pretty quick. Imagine the shock and mortification at hearing your lover yell out his ex’s name during sex! I’d smack him if I were Mari! Totally not acceptable.<br /><br />Anyway, the ending was great and I loved how all the pieces of the plot fit together neatly. Makes me want to grab the new books and start reading ASAP! <br /><br />Fave Quote:<br />"Missed you, witch. Ran headlong. Now hang up the bloody phone."<br />"Oh, great Hekate, is that his voice?" Carrow cried. "I just had an orgasm! Fudge your name tag if you have to, but get you some of that <i>some-some</i>. Remember, friends let friends live vicariously-"<br /><i> Click</i>. <br />pg. 284</span>
  <a data-text-id="13672308500207990291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1746071204683506009"><b>Reread Review August 5, 2017</b><br/><br/>5 "Ensorcelling" Stars!!<br/><br/>First off I have to say, I must have been much tougher with my reviews and ratings back in 2013, because this baby is getting an upgrade from 4 to 5 stars! <br/><br/>There is a damaged, angry, yet sweet possessive (in a good way), protective alpha male. (Lykae!) There is a super badass yet sweet and vulnerable female. They seem to have insurmountable obstacles to overcome. There is action, adventure, and romance. What else could a girl want in her PNR. N</span>
  <span id="freeText1746071204683506009" style="display:none"><b>Reread Review August 5, 2017</b><br /><br />5 "Ensorcelling" Stars!!<br /><br />First off I have to say, I must have been much tougher with my reviews and ratings back in 2013, because this baby is getting an upgrade from 4 to 5 stars! <br /><br />There is a damaged, angry, yet sweet possessive (in a good way), protective alpha male. (Lykae!) There is a super badass yet sweet and vulnerable female. They seem to have insurmountable obstacles to overcome. There is action, adventure, and romance. What else could a girl want in her PNR. Not too much if you ask me! Plus, I do love the wolves. Forever and always a wolf girl. 😉 <br /><br />Loving this reread! On to Conrad!! Happy reading!!<br /><br /><br /><b>Original Review May 2013</b><br /><br />I liked this one so much! I think this is my favorite IAD book so far. I adore Bowen and Mari. Both main character s were VERY strong personalities. This story felt so authentic to me (what does that say about me when this is a paranormal romance?). Anyway, the ending was perfect and everything worked out so well. My only question is what did Mari's tattoo mean? Did I miss that? I highly recommend this one for paranormal lovers. Happy reading!<br /><br />Oh, yea! I just have one little bad thing to say... these book covers are terrible! The next book has a much better cover. The next book has a ghost as the female lead. Interesting...</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126200874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5173462600883971540">WARNING! May cause insomnia and heart problems. Proceed with caution!<br/> <br/>Where’s the sixth circle for the vote when you need it?<br/><br/>I really don’t know how Kresley Cole can do this to me. Just when I thought this series can’t get better than No Rest for the Wicked, something extraordinary happened. Hmmm how should I put this? Oh yes! Imagine you’re walking down the street minding your own business when an alien dressed like Michael Jackson rushes by you and makes you fall to the ground. Pauses. Returns</span>
  <span id="freeText5173462600883971540" style="display:none">WARNING! May cause insomnia and heart problems. Proceed with caution!<br> <br>Where’s the sixth circle for the vote when you need it?<br><br>I really don’t know how Kresley Cole can do this to me. Just when I thought this series can’t get better than No Rest for the Wicked, something extraordinary happened. Hmmm how should I put this? Oh yes! Imagine you’re walking down the street minding your own business when an alien dressed like Michael Jackson rushes by you and makes you fall to the ground. Pauses. Returns, stomps all over you and then makes his escape while doing the Moonwalk. I felt exactly like that while reading Wicked Deeds on a Winter's Night. It actually topped the previous book, no doubt about it.<br><br>So, we have the best thing about it: a great story! I liked the way it gradually evolved; at first you would think it won’t be something spectacular but towards the end it left me breathless. I stayed up till 4 am to finish it. Worth every second, I’m telling you! The characters are amazing also. I did not like Bowen, especially since he was such an asshole in No Rest for the Wicked but I felt bad for him. Being mutilated and stuck in that inferno cannot be compared to, say, a little bit of torture. I would wish that to few people actually, and that shows Bowen had a bit of a chance to win back my heart. And oh man he did! Mariketa was a darling. She is a strong, intelligent woman. And also a very funny one. She made me laugh out loud many times. We also got glimpses on some new characters that I was sure will get their own books. After checking I saw that they did. Yei me! Cade in book 6 and Rydstrom in book 7. That’s some good news for today.<br><br>So here are a few images that show my reactions throughout the book: <br><br>At the beginning<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340457i/696844.jpg" width="300" height="336" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Half-way though<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340457i/696845.jpg" width="300" height="315" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Close to the end<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340457i/696846.jpg" width="300" height="226" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Before the epilogue<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340457i/696847.jpg" width="300" height="275" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That being said, here are some quotes I loved:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>Whenever other Lore creatures like the nymphs and satyrs turned their noses up at the “hex-hacks,” Carrow would raise both her hands in the rock-on horns gesture and shout, “Double, double, toil and trouble, muthafuckas! You just got cursed!”<br>Then she actually would curse them.<br><br>Nïx lay on her side, bending her elbow to casually prop her head in her hand. With a sigh she said, “Bowen, I took you on as my pet project because I like to ogle you. Due to your rowr factor.”<br><br>“She, too, is one of Regin’s friends. They’re poker buddies, sisters of the Wii, and Mari is a vaunted member of the karaoke contingent. Regin has long acted as the witches’ designated driver.” “BFF?” Lachlain asked, brows drawn. “Sisters of the what?”<br>Emma supplied, “Best friend forever and a video game.”<br>Lachlain muttered to Emma, “Your relatives are just no’ right.”<br><br>“What’s your favorite place to visit?” He absently answered, “Wherever you are.”<br>“Bowen, five things about you can’t all be about me.”<br>But you’re the only good thing that I’ve got.<br><br>In the mud, she’d written him a note with precise letters.<br>Fuckhead:<br>The name’s MariKETA.<br>Go to hell,<br>The WITCH, doing a creepy spell somewhere right now. </i>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716287357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11934225572229741153">I have no idea why this one got such a high rating. It sucked ass. It's the worst of the lot. Though, yeah, I skipped the book before it.<br/><br/>The couple in this book just didn't do anything for me. It was a combination of my problem with the first book (ie. the hell I'm going to believe any woman would actually love a man who kidnapped and nearly rapes her every time he sees her) but this one went up a notch from there. <br/><br/>Where to start?<br/><br/>There's no love between them at all. Throughout the whole book. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText11934225572229741153" style="display:none">I have no idea why this one got such a high rating. It sucked ass. It's the worst of the lot. Though, yeah, I skipped the book before it.<br /><br />The couple in this book just didn't do anything for me. It was a combination of my problem with the first book (ie. the hell I'm going to believe any woman would actually love a man who kidnapped and nearly rapes her every time he sees her) but this one went up a notch from there. <br /><br />Where to start?<br /><br />There's no love between them at all. Throughout the whole book. The only time they actually mention love is in the last chapter. Bleh. <br /><br />We have Bow who is horrible, horrible to her. He accuses her of hexing him because he wants her. After attempting to rape her, he accuses her of this before stealing what she helped him to get and locked him in a place where she almost died (while being surrounded by monsters.)<br /><br />And you know what the inducement had to be to get him to 'rescue' her? A war that would've killed his entire species.<br /><br />Oh! Be still my burning heart!<br /><br />After he rescues her, he then decides that she must be his mate so he insta-loves her again. Insta-love with him absolutely hating everything that she is. This, of course, doesn't change at all until she almost dies and her power saves them. <br /><br />Wow. That's one for the history books!<br /><br />And, as if this wasn't all bad enough, you get hit with the cliche 'from weakest character in the world to strongest goddamn thing that can kill gods after training for a week' cliche. I noticed this in the first book but it was more believable because the ubber villain wanted to die. This one, not so much.<br /><br />There was no love here. The sex was really cringe worthy too. He goes from trying to kill her to 'let's fuck because why not?' in less than a couple hours. It was repulsive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11934225572229741153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/2367556-kathleen">Kathleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262839275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14585578239726913028">Story Rating 5 stars<br/>Character Rating 5 stars<br/>Romance Rating 4.5 stars<br/>Imagination 5 stars<br/>Heat Level 3 stars<br/>Action Level 5 stars<br/>Overall Rating 5 stars<br/>Favorite Character, Mariketa<br/><br/>This book started out with lots of action that grabbed me right from the start. This part of the book's setting took place during The Talisman's Hie competition which also took place in the pervious book No Rest For The Wicked. This story kind of felt like Romancing the Stone entwined with Raiders Of The Lost Arc gone paran</span>
  <span id="freeText14585578239726913028" style="display:none">Story Rating 5 stars<br />Character Rating 5 stars<br />Romance Rating 4.5 stars<br />Imagination 5 stars<br />Heat Level 3 stars<br />Action Level 5 stars<br />Overall Rating 5 stars<br />Favorite Character, Mariketa<br /><br />This book started out with lots of action that grabbed me right from the start. This part of the book's setting took place during The Talisman's Hie competition which also took place in the pervious book No Rest For The Wicked. This story kind of felt like Romancing the Stone entwined with Raiders Of The Lost Arc gone paranormal. Once again this had some of the best imagination I've read to date.<br /><br />Right from the start the heroine Mariketa was drawn to Bowen. Bowen struggled with his attraction to Mari because he wanted to stay loyal to his mate who had died long ago. They end up doing some rather nasty things to each other for reason I won't get into.<br /><br />When the full moon rises and Bowen can't stay away he hunts Mari down. What happens next is very gruesome and scares Mari but once his beast settles down and she finally realizes just what she means to him, the mating begin's and let me tell you this was very HOT.<br /><br />The end battle between Mari and the evil sorceress Haxa's was yet another very exciting part that ultimately gave the story it's HEA ending. I really hope we get some glimpses of Mari and Bowen in the following book's.<br /><br />Mari was my favorite character because there was just so much imagination put into her character. Once again I'm not going to get into it. I just have to say that if you love your reads with a lot an excellent story telling filled with phenomenal imagination, great characters, Lot's of action and a steamy romance you really should read this series.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1741624588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2927143490022095933">Oh. Well, it’s funny how as you are reading a book you feel a certain way right? For like, the whole book almost. Then, boom, out of nowhere it all changes. Yep, that is what happened to me with this one.<br/><br/>Mari drove me crazy. Yes, I know she is young. I mean, really, really young. She is only 23. Not yet immortal so yeah, ONLY 23, for realsies. But OMG she drove me crazy.<br/><br/>I couldn’t wait to read Bowen’s book and really, his story lived up to what I wanted for him…mostly. Mari drove me crazy.<br/><br/>I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText2927143490022095933" style="display:none">Oh. Well, it’s funny how as you are reading a book you feel a certain way right? For like, the whole book almost. Then, boom, out of nowhere it all changes. Yep, that is what happened to me with this one.<br /><br />Mari drove me crazy. Yes, I know she is young. I mean, really, really young. She is only 23. Not yet immortal so yeah, ONLY 23, for realsies. But OMG she drove me crazy.<br /><br />I couldn’t wait to read Bowen’s book and really, his story lived up to what I wanted for him…mostly. Mari drove me crazy.<br /><br />I think out of all the creatures in the world witches are my absolute favorite and as I turned page after page I just felt so much frustration. The cat and mouse game that is a theme within these books was taken to a whole different level with this one. I didn’t know if I could stand much more. Not to mention the itsy bitsy (mostly) mistakes Bowen kept making. All of it just seemed too much this go round.<br /><br />And then BOOM!<br /><br />Holy moly. The last 15% or so was so very exciting I couldn’t seem to turn the pages fast enough. I was tricked! I was deceived! AND IT WAS AWESOME!!! My head was spinning and it felt so very good!<br /><br />So, I would say that for 85% of this book I just chalked this one up as a fail and then out of nowhere it truly became one I’ll probably remember the most.<br /><br />Love when that happens honestly.<br /><br />Mari still drove me crazy.<br /><br />Whose next?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2927143490022095933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DfeL+SJQfms3r5oPmS0baIl/mUHjgDSYJiOcp6ZBHDo0gKrRK/2h7qlpA+DV9IR1k9xZxYQNYc0opfQQ/M7rCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Disarmed, he invites her to spend the journey to St. Louis in his private car—perhaps against his better judgment. \n\nClara Dawson has long known how to take care of herself, but the savvy shop girl is at a loss when she witnesses—and becomes entangled in—a terrible crime. <span id="freeTextContainer11073399024472990944">Kresley Cole is the #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of the electrifying Immortals After Dark paranormal series, the young adult Arcana Chronicles series, the erotic Gamemakers series, and five award-winning historical romances.<br/><br/>A master’s grad and former athlete, she has traveled over much of the world and draws from those experiences to create her memorable characters and settings. <br/>Her IAD bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11073399024472990944" style="display:none">Kresley Cole is the #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of the electrifying Immortals After Dark paranormal series, the young adult Arcana Chronicles series, the erotic Gamemakers series, and five award-winning historical romances.<br /><br />A master’s grad and former athlete, she has traveled over much of the world and draws from those experiences to create her memorable characters and settings. <br />Her IAD books have been translated into 23 foreign languages, garnered three RITA awards, a RWA Hall of Fame induction, and consistently appear on the bestseller lists, in the U.S. and abroad.<br /><br />Cole lives in Florida with her family. Learn more about Kresley at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kresleycole.com">www.kresleycole.com</a> &amp; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thearcanachronicles.com">www.thearcanachronicles.com</a><br /><br /></span>
